## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Cross-Org WebIDL to DOM Binding Discovery

## Your Task

Find all WebIDL interface files in `mozilla-firefox/firefox` under `dom/webidl/` that define DOM interfaces for the Fetch API (Request, Response, Headers, FetchEvent). Then find the corresponding C++ binding implementation files under `dom/fetch/` that implement these WebIDL interfaces. Report the WebIDL file, the C++ header, and the C++ implementation file for each Fetch API type.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

## Summary

I've mapped all four Fetch API interfaces to their WebIDL and C++ implementation files:

**Request Interface**
- WebIDL: `dom/webidl/Request.webidl`
- Header: `dom/fetch/Request.h`
- Implementation: `dom/fetch/Request.cpp`

**Response Interface**
- WebIDL: `dom/webidl/Response.webidl`
- Header: `dom/fetch/Response.h`
- Implementation: `dom/fetch/Response.cpp`

**Headers Interface**
- WebIDL: `dom/webidl/Headers.webidl`
- Header: `dom/fetch/Headers.h`
- Implementation: `dom/fetch/Headers.cpp`

**FetchEvent Interface**
- WebIDL: `dom/webidl/FetchEvent.webidl`
- Header: `dom/serviceworkers/ServiceWorkerEvents.h`
- Implementation: `dom/serviceworkers/ServiceWorkerEvents.cpp`

ExtendableEvent\\n  Includes FetchEventBinding.h for WebIDL bindings\\n  Manages fetch interception, response handling, and the promise-based respondWith mechanism\\n- **C++ Implementation**: dom/serviceworkers/ServiceWorkerEvents.cpp\\n  Implements the FetchEvent interface methods and lifecycle\\n  Handles service worker fetch interception and event dispatching\\n\\n## Architecture Notes\\n\\n1. **WebIDL Binding Files**: While not listed as separate files, the binding headers (RequestBinding.h, ResponseBinding.h, HeadersBinding.h, FetchEventBinding.h) are auto-generated from the WebIDL files and provide the glue code between JavaScript and C++.\\n\\n2. **Internal Classes**: Many Fetch API implementations use internal classes:\\n   - InternalRequest (used by Request)\\n   - InternalResponse (used by Response)\\n   - InternalHeaders (used by Headers)\\n   These separate the public API from internal implementation details.\\n\\n3. **File Organization**: \\n   - Request, Response, and Headers implementations are located in dom/fetch/ as they are core Fetch API types\\n   - FetchEvent is located in dom/serviceworkers/ as it is part of the Service Worker specification\\n\\n4. **Binding Pattern**: All classes follow the pattern of:\\n   - Including their auto-generated *Binding.h header\\n   - Implementing a WrapObject method that uses the binding's Wrap function\\n   - Using nsWrapperCache to manage JavaScript object associations\"\n}\n",
